Ruling on Sale, Gift, and Mortgage of Mudabbar
States Hanafi prohibition and refutes Shafi'i evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi prohibition of selling a mudabbar and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Ibn Umar and critique of the Jabir report.

Core Idea
A mudabbar cannot be sold: the hadith of Ibn Umar is explicit, and the Shafi'i evidence is reinterpreted as a case of restricted tadbir or hire.

This passage presents a fierce inter-madhhab dispute over the legal status of a mudabbar – a slave whose emancipation is tied to the master's death. The Hanafi school holds that such a slave cannot be sold, given, or mortgaged, while the Shafi'i school permits it. The text provides the Hanafi proof from a hadith of Ibn Umar and then rebuts the Shafi'i reliance on the hadith of Jabir, using careful textual analysis and historical context. By working through this dispute, you will learn how different schools weigh evidence and how a single narration can be reinterpreted to resolve apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the mudabbar cannot be sold, given as a gift, or mortgaged. Note that this is the Hanafi position ('عندنا').
The ruling is absolute – no exceptions for debt or need.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
The Shafi'i school argues that tadbir is a conditional suspension like any other, and thus does not prevent sale. They cite the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet apparently sold a mudabbar.
The Shafi'i also analogize tadbir to a bequest (wasaya).
3
Examine the Hanafi proof – the hadith of Ibn Umar
The Hanafi rely on the explicit hadith: 'The mudabbar is not sold, not given, not inherited, and he is free from the third.' This is a clear prohibition.
The text defends the authenticity of this hadith, calling it mashhur (famous) and citing authorities who used it.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi school argues that the Jabir report is a case report (hikayat hal) with multiple possible interpretations: the slave may have been a restricted mudabbar (which is permissible to sell by consensus), or the transaction was a hire (called 'sale' in Yemeni dialect). They also note that the hadith may be abrogated.
This step shows how Hanafi usul handles conflicting evidence by reinterpretation and prioritization.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Under Hanafi law, a mudabbar enjoys protection from sale during the master's life. Under Shafi'i law, the master may sell him freely.
This difference affects the rights of the slave and the master's estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يرهن وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي له: يجوز إخراجه عن الملك بالبيع والهبة وغيرهما؛ لأن التدبير تعليق العتق بالشرط فلا يمنع به البيع والهبة كما في سائر التعليقات وكما في المدبر المقيد؛ ولأن التدبير وصية وهي غير مانعة من ذلك؛ لما روي عن جابر الله أن رجلاً أعتق غلاماً له عن دبر منه، فاحتاج، فأخذه النبي الله فقال : " من : يشتريه مني؟ فاشتراه نعيم ابن عبد الله بكذا وكذا، فدفعه إليه، متفق عليه"، وعن أحمد إنما يجوز بيعه إذا كان على السيد دين وعند مالك: لا يجوز بيعه حال الحياة، ويجوز بعد الممات إن كان على المولى دين، ولنا ما رواه ابن عمر لما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إن المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث، وهو حر من الثلث"، فإن قلت: الحديث غريب ولو اشتهر حمل على نفي الفضيلة ونحن نقول به؟ قلت: الحديث مشهور احتج به الكر. والطحاوي والرازي وغيرهم من ا الأئمة، وروى أبو الوليد الباجي أن عمر ه رد بیع القرون وهم حضور متوافرون وهو إجماع منهم أن بيع المدبر لا يجوز، وما رواه الشافعي حكاية حال، فلا يمكن الاحتجاج به؛ لأنه يحتمل أن يكون الغلام مدبراً مقيداً، ويحتمل أنه باع صفته بأن آجره، والإجارة تسمى بيعاً بلغة أهل اليمن؛ لأن فيها بيع المنفعة، يؤيده ما رواه جابر أنه عليه باع خدمة المدبر، ذكره أبو الوليد المالكي أنه باع في وقت كان يباع الحر بالديون كما روي أنه عليه باع حر حراً بدينه، ثم نسخ بقوله تعالى: وَإِنْ كَانَ ذُو عُسْرَةٍ فَنَظِرَةٌ إِلَى مَيْسَرَةٍ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۸۰) ذكره في الناسخ والمنسوخ.
So he cannot be sold, nor given as gift, nor mortgaged – and this is with us (Hanafis). Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible to remove him from ownership by sale, gift, etc., because tadbir is suspension of emancipation upon a condition, so it does not prevent sale and gift like other suspensions and like the restricted mudabbar; and because tadbir is a bequest, which does not prevent that, due to what is narrated from Jabir that a man emancipated his slave from his back (mudabbar), then became needy, so the Prophet (saw) took him and said: 'Who will buy him from me?' So Nu'aym ibn Abdillah bought him for such and such, and gave it to him – agreed upon. And from Ahmad: It is only permissible to sell him if the master has debt. And with Malik: It is not permissible to sell him during life, but permissible after death if the master has debt. Our proof is what Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet (saw) said: 'Indeed the mudabbar is not sold, nor given, nor inherited, and he is free from the third.' If you say: The hadith is gharib (rare), and even if famous it would be interpreted as negation of virtue, and we hold that? I say: The hadith is mashhur (famous); it was used as proof by al-K., al-Tahawi, al-Razi and other imams. And Abu al-Walid al-Baji narrated that Umar rejected the sale of al-Qurun while they were numerous attendees, and it is a consensus from them that sale of mudabbar is not permissible. And what al-Shafi'i narrated is a case report (hikayat hal), so it cannot be used as proof because it is possible the boy was a restricted mudabbar, and possible that he sold his services by hiring him, and hiring is called sale in the language of Yemen because it involves sale of benefit. This is supported by what Jabir narrated that he sold the service of the mudabbar. It is mentioned by Abu al-Walid al-Maliki that he sold at a time when free men were sold for debts, as it is narrated that he sold a free man for his debt, then it was abrogated by Allah's saying: 'And if someone is in hardship, then postponement until ease' (Baqarah 280). Mentioned in al-Nasikh wal-Mansukh.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of selling, gifting, or mortgaging a mudabbar (a slave who has been given a tadbir). The Hanafi position (stated as 'عندنا') is that these transactions are absolutely prohibited. The Shafi'i school allows them, arguing that tadbir is a conditional emancipation and thus no different from other conditional suspensions, and that it is like a bequest which does not restrict ownership. They cite the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet apparently sold a mudabbar. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, they present a hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly stating the prohibition. Second, they refute the Shafi'i evidence by arguing that the incident may have involved a restricted mudabbar (whose sale is allowed by consensus) or that the 'sale' was actually a hire (since the Yemeni dialect uses 'sale' for hire). They also mention that the hadith of Jabir is abrogated by the Quranic verse on postponement for debtors. The text also notes positions of Ahmad and Malik. The Hanafi proof is considered strong with consensus of some companions.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is tied to the master's death.
تدبير مقيد (tadbir muqayyad): Tadbir restricted to a specific condition like a particular journey or illness.
حكاية حال (hikayat hal): A report describing a specific incident without a general ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling a mudabbar?
A) Permissible with the master's permission
B) Permissible only if the master is in debt
C) Prohibited and invalid
D) Permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar is protected from sale because the hadith of Ibn Umar and companion consensus establish an explicit prohibition that outweighs the Shafi'i case report.

Consequences of Tadbir Upon Master's Death
Explains permissible uses of mudabbar and the rule upon master's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences of a valid tadbir upon the master's death, including the mudabbar's obligations when the estate is insufficient or in debt.

Core Idea
Upon master's death, mudabbar is freed from one-third; must work for remainder if no other assets or if debt exists.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the practical outcomes of tadbir. While the mudabbar remains a slave during the master's life, his status changes at death. The discussion centers on how the bequest (tadbir) interacts with inheritance and debt, and what obligations fall on the mudabbar when the estate is insufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tadbir (a master declaring a slave mudabbar). The default ruling upon the master's death is that the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate.
The mudabbar remains a slave during the master's life.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'He is free from the third' and the analogy that tadbir is a bequest, which is executed from one-third.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly limits the freedom to 'the third', indicating that the mudabbar is not freed from the entire estate. The analogy to bequest reinforces this limit.
The phrase 'من الثلث' is the operative part.
4
Analyze the practical cases
If the master has no other property, the mudabbar works for two-thirds of his value. If the master's debt covers the entire estate, the mudabbar works for his full value.
Debt takes precedence over bequest; emancipation is not nullified but is satisfied through payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستخدم ويؤجر، وتوطأ وتنكح، وبموته عتق من ثلثه أي فإذا مات المولى عتق المدبر من ثلث ماله؛ لما روينا عن قوله عليه: "وهو حر من الثلث"؛ ولأن التدبير وصية؛ لأنه تبرع مضاف إلى وقت الموت والحكم غير ثابت في الحال فينفذ من الثلث، فلو لم يكن له مال غيره سعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته وقوله: "كله" بالجر عطف على "ثلثيه"، أي وإن كان المولى ماله مديوناً بدين محيط بجميع المدبر في كل قيمته؛ لأن الدين مقدم على الوصية، ولا يمكن نقض العتق؛ لأنه غير مشروع، فيجب نقضه معنى برد قيمته. (مستخلص عيني لو فقيراً: أي لو كان المولى فقيراً و لم يكن ماله غيره. (عيني) سعى
He (the mudabbar) may be employed and hired out; the female mudabbar may be cohabited with and married off. Upon his death he is freed from one-third, meaning when the master dies the mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth, due to what we narrated from his saying (saw): 'He is free from the third.' And because tadbir is a bequest, since it is a donation attached to the time of death and the ruling is not established at present, so it is executed from the third. If he has no other wealth, the mudabbar works for two-thirds of his value. And his saying 'all of it' (in the text) is in the genitive, conjoined to 'two-thirds' meaning if the master's wealth is all of it covered by debt, then the mudabbar is required to work for his entire value, because debt takes precedence over the bequest, and the emancipation cannot be nullified because it is not legislated, so it must be nullified in meaning by returning his value. (Mustakhlas, Ayni) 'If he is poor': meaning if the master is poor and has no other wealth. (Ayni) He works.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof passage covering the practical consequences of tadbir. First, the mudabbar (or mudabbarah) remains usable: the master may employ him, hire him out, and if female, the master may cohabit with her or marry her off. This is because ownership is intact. Second, upon the master's death, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate, based on the hadith that the mudabbar is 'free from the third' and because tadbir is a bequest effective after death. If the master has no other property, the mudabbar must work to compensate the heirs for two-thirds of his value (since only one-third can be bequeathed). If the master is in debt exceeding the entire value of the mudabbar, the mudabbar must work to pay the entire value because debts have priority over bequests. The emancipation is not invalidated, but the mudabbar must pay his value to the creditors.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the master's estate, the maximum portion from which tadbir can be executed.
سعى (sa'a): The mudabbar works or earns to pay off a portion of his value to the heirs or creditors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master dies with no other property except a mudabbar, what happens?
A) The mudabbar is freed entirely
B) The mudabbar is freed from one-third and must work for two-thirds of his value
C) The mudabbar remains a slave permanently
D) The mudabbar is freed from half of his value

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's estate upon death; if the estate is insufficient, he must work to compensate the heirs or creditors.

The Time-Bound Tadbir and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on time-bound tadbir classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the chosen Hanafi position (Hasan ibn Ziyad) to classify a time-bound tadbir as muqayyad or mutlaq and state whether the mudabbar can be sold.

Core Idea
If a tadbir condition is virtually inevitable, the slave becomes an absolute mudabbar and cannot be sold.

When a master ties a slave's emancipation to a condition like death from a specific illness, the tadbir is restricted and the slave can be sold by consensus. However, when the condition is a long timeframe such as a hundred years, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Yusuf and establishes the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default classification
Recognize what the master said: if it is tied to a specific attribute (e.g., 'this illness'), it is a restricted tadbir; the slave can be sold by consensus because the condition is uncertain.
2
Recognize the disputed scenario
When the condition is a long timeframe (e.g., 'within 100 years'), two views emerge among Hanafi scholars: does it remain restricted or become absolute?
3
Understand the reasoning of each side
Hasan ibn Ziyad argues that if the master would not normally outlive that period, the condition is virtually inevitable, so it is absolute. Abu Yusuf insists that the explicit time limit maintains the restriction.
4
Apply the chosen position
The text declares 'al-mukhtar huwa al-awwal' – the chosen view is Hasan's. If the timeframe is such that the master is unlikely to survive it, the tadbir becomes absolute and sale is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباع لو قال: هذا شروع في بيان حكم المدبر المقيد يعني إذا قال لعبده إن مت من مرضي هذا أو في سفري هذا فأنت حر، أو قال: إن مت إلى عشر سنين فأنت حر فليس بمدبر مطلق بل هو مدبر مقيد يجوز بيعه بالإجماع؛ لأن السبب لم ينعقد في الحال؛ لتردده في تلك الصفة، بخلاف المدير المطلق؛ لأن عتقه تعلق بالموت، وقيد بعشر سنين؛ لأنه لو قال: إلى مائة سنة، ومثله لا يعيش إليه غالباً فهو مدبر مطلق عند الحسن ابن زياد، وقال أبو يوسف: ليس بمطلق؛ لأن العبرة للتوقيت، والمختار هو الأول؛ لأنه إذا كان في الغالب لا يعيش إليه يصير كالكائن لا محالة، فلا يجوز بيعه مستخلص، عيني، فتح)
And it is sold if he said: This is the beginning of explaining the ruling of the restricted mudabbar. Meaning, if he said to his slave 'if I die from this illness of mine' or 'on this journey of mine you are free', or he said 'if I die within ten years you are free', then he is not an absolute mudabbar but a restricted mudabbar, and his sale is permissible by consensus, because the cause is not in effect due to its uncertainty in that attribute, unlike the absolute mudabbar. Because his emancipation is tied to death, and he restricted it to ten years. For if he said 'within one hundred years' and generally he does not live that long, then it is absolute mudabbar according to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Abu Yusuf said it is not absolute because the consideration is the timelimit. The chosen (mukhtar) is the first (Hasan's view), because if he generally does not live that long, it becomes like the inevitable, so his sale is not permissible. (Mustakhlas, Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of a time-bound tadbir when the timeframe is very long (e.g., a hundred years). The passage begins by stating the rule for restricted tadbir (muqayyad): when the master ties emancipation to a specific condition like a particular illness or journey, it is a restricted tadbir, and by consensus the mudabbar can be sold because the condition is uncertain. However, when the condition is a long timeframe such as 'within a hundred years', two views emerge. Imam al-Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it an absolute tadbir because the master will most likely die within that time, making the condition virtually inevitable. Imam Abu Yusuf considers it still restricted because the explicit time limit matters (al-ibra lil-tawqit). The text states that the chosen (mukhtar) position is that of Hasan ibn Ziyad, meaning the slave becomes an absolute mudabbar and cannot be sold. This is because if the condition is almost certain to occur, it is treated as inevitable.

Key Terms
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A slave whose tadbir is tied to a specific condition, e.g., death from a particular illness.
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar mutlaq): A slave whose tadbir is tied to death absolutely, without condition.
الغالبة (al-ghalaba): Customary certainty; overwhelming probability that a condition will occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen Hanafi position, a tadbir conditioned on the master's death within 100 years is treated as:
A) Restricted, so sale is allowed
B) Absolute, so sale is not allowed
C) Void because the condition is unlikely
D) Dependent on the master's intention

Key Takeaway
When a tadbir condition is so long that the master would not normally outlive it, the condition is treated as inevitable, making the slave an absolute mudabbar who cannot be sold.

The Prohibition of Selling a Mudabbar: Hanafi Proof and Refutation of Opposing Views
Explains general tadbir rulings and refutes Shafi'i/Maliki on sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar, cite the primary dalil (hadith and ijma), and explain why the opposing narrations are either misinterpretations or abrogated.

Core Idea
The mudabbar cannot be sold – the Prophet's hadith and Companion consensus establish a complete prohibition.

This lesson examines the legal status of a mudabbar (a slave declared free upon the master's death). While the mudabbar can be used, rented, and (if female) married or cohabited, the Hanafi school maintains that he cannot be sold, given as a gift, or pawned. We will analyze the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, the claim of ijma, and the Hanafi response to reports that seem to allow sale. Understanding this dispute clarifies the boundary between ownership and future freedom in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its scope
State explicitly that the sale of a mudabbar is prohibited (haram) absolutely, while other dispositions like hiring, using, and marrying off are allowed. Note the exception: if the master dies with only the mudabbar as asset, the slave must work to pay two-thirds of his value to heirs (or all if debt exists).
The prohibition is derived from hadith and ijma.
2
Examine the primary proof – the hadith of Ibn Umar
Look at the text: 'إن المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث، وهو حر من الثلث'. The explicit negation (لا يباع) indicates a prohibition. This hadith is ahad but considered famous (mashhur) among Hanafis and relied upon by major imams. Also note the Companion consensus (ijma) reported by Abu al-Walid al-Baji from Umar's rejection of sale.
The Hanafi position on thubut zanni and dalala zanni is acceptable for obligation/prohibition in non-essentials.
3
Evaluate the opposing views
Ahmad permits sale only if the master has debt; Malik prohibits sale during life but allows it after death if debt exists. Their evidence includes incidents where the Prophet allegedly sold a mudabbar or a free man for debt.
These incidents are reported by al-Shafi'i and others.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi commentator argues that those incidents are: (a) possibly about a restricted mudabbar (mudabbar muqayyad) or (b) actually a lease (ijara) – the word 'sale' may be used in Yemeni dialect for lease. Moreover, the story of selling a free man for debt is abrogated by Quran 2:280 (postponement). Thus they do not contradict the general prohibition.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of defending the primary proof through interpretation and abrogation.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: a creditor cannot force the sale of a mudabbar even if the master has no other assets. Maliki: after the master's death, if there is debt, the mudabbar may be sold. Ahmad: even during life, if debt exists, sale is allowed. The difference affects the rights of creditors and heirs.

ويستخدم ويؤجر، وتوطأ وتنكح، وبموته عتق من ثلثه في ثلثيه لو فقيراً، وسعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته. أحمد إنما يجوز بيعه إذا كان على السيد دين وعند مالك: لا يجوز بيعه حال الحياة، ويجوز بعد الممات إن كان على المولى دين، ولنا ما رواه ابن عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إن المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث، وهو حر من الثلث"، فإن قلت: الحديث غريب ولو اشتهر حمل على نفي الفضيلة ونحن نقول به؟ قلت: الحديث مشهور احتج به الكر. والطحاوي والرازي وغيرهم من الأئمة، وروى أبو الوليد الباجي أن عمر رد بيع القرون وهم حضور متوافرون وهو إجماع منهم أن بيع المدبر لا يجوز، وما رواه الشافعي حكاية حال، فلا يمكن الاحتجاج به؛ لأنه يحتمل أن يكون الغلام مدبراً مقيداً، ويحتمل أنه باع صفته بأن آجره، والإجارة تسمى بيعاً بلغة أهل اليمن؛ لأن فيها بيع المنفعة، يؤيده ما رواه جابر أنه عليه باع خدمة المدبر، ذكره أبو الوليد المالكي أنه باع في وقت كان يباع الحر بالديون كما روي أنه عليه باع حراً بدينه، ثم نسخ بقوله تعالى: {وَإِن كَانَ ذُو عُسْرَةٍ فَنَظِرَةٌ إِلَى مَيْسَرَةٍ} [البقرة: 280] ذكره في الناسخ والمنسوخ. ويستخدم ويؤجر: أي استخدم المدبر وإجارة وطء المولى المدبرة وترويجها يجوز بالإجماع؛ لأن الملك ثابت فيه وبالملك تستفاد ولاية هذه التصرفات بخلاف البيع ونحوه، فإنه يبطل حقه فيه فلا يملك، وليس له أن يرهنه؛ لأن موجب الرهن ثبوت يد الاستيفاء من المالية بطريق البيع، وهو ليس محلا للبيع كأم الولد. وبموته عتق من ثلثه أي فإذا مات المولى عتق المدبر من ثلث ماله؛ لما روينا عن قوله عليه: "وهو حر من الثلث"؛ ولأن التدبير وصية؛ لأنه تبرع مضاف إلى وقت الموت والحكم غير ثابت في الحال فينفذ من الثلث، فلو لم يكن له مال غيره سعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته وقوله: "كله" بالجر عطف على "ثلثيه"، أي وإن كان المولى ماله مديوناً بدين محيط بجميع المدبر في كل قيمته؛ لأن الدين مقدم على الوصية، ولا يمكن نقض العتق؛ لأنه غير مشروع، فيجب نقضه معنى برد قيمته.
He is used and rented, and she is cohabited and married off, and upon his death he is freed from his third, in his two-thirds if he is poor, and the mudabbar works to earn two-thirds of his value. Ahmad said: He may be sold only if the master has debt, and according to Malik: He may not be sold during life, but may be sold after death if the master has debt. Our proof is what Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The mudabbar is not sold, not given as a gift, and not inherited; he is free from the third.' If you say: The hadith is ghareeb and even if famous, it is interpreted as negating virtue, and we agree? I say: The hadith is famous, argued by al-Kara [al-Karkhi?] and al-Tahawi and al-Razi and other imams, and Abu al-Walid al-Baji narrated that Umar rejected the sale of Quroon while many were present, and it is consensus that sale of mudabbar is not allowed. What al-Shafi'i narrated is a singular incident, so it cannot be used as evidence; because it is possible the slave was a restricted mudabbar, or he sold his benefit by leasing him, and leasing is called sale in the language of Yemen because it involves sale of benefit. Supporting this is what Jabir narrated that he sold the service of a mudabbar, mentioned by Abu al-Walid al-Maliki that he sold at a time when free people were sold for debts, as narrated that he sold a free person for his debt, then abrogated by His statement: {And if someone is in hardship, then postponement to ease} [2:280] as mentioned in al-Nasikh wal-Mansukh. He is used and rented: meaning using the mudabbar and leasing and the master cohabiting with the female mudabbar and marrying her off is permissible by consensus; because ownership is established over him, and through ownership authority over these actions is derived, unlike sale and similar, because it invalidates his right in him so he does not own. He may not pawn him because the requirement of pawn is establishing a right of financial recovery by way of sale, and he is not subject to sale like umm al-walad. Upon his death he is freed from his third: meaning when the master dies, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth; due to what we narrated from his statement: 'He is free from the third'; and because tadbir is a will; because it is a donation attached to the time of death and the ruling is not established at present, so it is executed from the third. If he has no other wealth, the mudabbar works to earn two-thirds of his value. His statement 'kullih' (all of it) is in genitive, conjoined to 'thalathayhi', meaning if the master's wealth is entirely consumed by debt, the mudabbar works for all his value; because debt precedes the will, and rescinding the emancipation is not permitted, so it must be rescinded effectively by returning his value.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a combination of matn, inter-madhhab dispute, and commentary. It begins with the general rulings of the mudabbar (a slave declared free upon the master's death). The matn states: he may be used for labor, rented out, the female mudabbar may be cohabited and married off. Upon the master's death, he is freed from one-third of the master's wealth; if the master is poor (the only asset is the mudabbar), the slave must work to pay two-thirds of his value to the heirs. The commentator then introduces a dispute on selling the mudabbar. Imam Ahmad permits sale only if the master has debt; Imam Malik prohibits sale during the master's life but permits it after death if there is debt. The Hanafi position (from Abu Hanifa) prohibits sale entirely, based on a hadith narrated by Ibn Umar that the mudabbar cannot be sold, given as a gift, or inherited; he is free from one-third. The commentator addresses an objection: the hadith is strange (ghareeb) and even if known, it might be interpreted as negating virtue (i.e., it is not commendable to sell). He responds that the hadith is famous and used as evidence by major Hanafi scholars; moreover, there is consensus (ijma) of the Companions as reported by Abu al-Walid al-Baji from Umar. As for the Shafi'i narration, it is a specific incident that may be interpreted as selling a restricted mudabbar or as a lease (which is called 'sale' in Yemeni dialect), so it does not disprove the general prohibition. The commentary then expands on the matn: using, renting, and marriage are allowed because ownership is intact, but sale would invalidate that ownership. The mudabbar cannot be pawned because pawning implies eventual sale, which is not permitted for the mudabbar (like umm al-walad). Upon death, emancipation is from the third because tadbir is a will; if debt exists, the mudabbar must work to pay the debt before emancipation.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration that a slave is free upon the master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been declared free upon the master's death.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling a mudabbar?
A) Permissible if the master consents.
B) Prohibited absolutely, based on hadith and ijma.
C) Prohibited only if the master has no debt.
D) Makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar is a unique category: he can be used and rented, but cannot be sold, because his status as a future free person, established by a will, takes precedence over transactional ownership.

Sale of the Restricted Mudabbar and the 100-Year Condition
Expands on the matn's ruling on restricted tadbir and its sale, including an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between restricted and absolute tadbir regarding saleability, and apply the preferred Hanafi ruling when the condition is practically impossible.

Core Idea
A restricted mudabbar can be sold; but if the condition is almost certain, it becomes absolute and cannot be sold.

In this passage, the author clarifies that when a master makes tadbir conditional on a specific attribute (like a particular illness), the slave is a restricted mudabbar. The key consequence is that such a slave can be sold, unlike an absolute mudabbar. However, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the condition is extremely long (e.g., 100 years): does it become absolute? Let's explore the reasoning and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on sale
State the general rule: a restricted mudabbar can be sold by consensus. Contrast with absolute tadbir where sale is prohibited.
The text says 'يجوز بيعه بالإجماع'.
2
Understand the rationale
The cause (sabab) is not concluded immediately because it is conditional on a specific attribute, so the slave is not fully mudabbar yet.
Reason: 'السبب لم ينعقد في الحال'.
3
Analyze the 100-year condition dispute
If the master says 'if I die within 100 years', Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it absolute tadbir (no sale), while Abu Yusuf says it remains restricted (sale allowed). Examine both arguments.
Hasan: condition practically inevitable. Abu Yusuf: consideration to wording.
4
Determine the preferred view
The preferred view (mukhtar) is that of Hasan ibn Ziyad: if the condition is unlikely to occur, it becomes as if inevitable, so the slave is absolute mudabbar and cannot be sold.
Tarjih by al-Ayni and others.
5
Apply the rule
Given a scenario (e.g., master says 'if I die within 200 years'), decide whether the slave can be sold. Apply the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباع لو قال: هذا شروع في بيان حكم المدبر المقيد يعني إذا قال لعبده إن مت من مرضي هذا أو في سفري هذا فأنت حر، أو قال: إن مت إلى عشر سنين فأنت حر فليس بمدبر مطلق بل هو مدبر مقيد يجوز بيعه بالإجماع؛ لأن السبب لم ينعقد في الحال؛ لتردده في تلك الصفة، بخلاف المدبر المطلق؛ لأن عتقه تعلق بالموت، وقيد بعشر سنين؛ لأنه لو قال: إلى مائة سنة، ومثله لا يعيش إليه غالباً فهو مدبر مطلق عند الحسن ابن زياد، وقال أبو يوسف: ليس بمطلق؛ لأن العبرة للتوقيت، والمختار هو الأول؛ لأنه إذا كان في الغالب لا يعيش إليه يصير كالكائن لا محالة، فلا يجوز بيعه. أو إلى عشر سنين: أي أو قال: إن مت إلى عشر سنين فأنت حر. أو أنت حر بعد موت فلان: أي لو قال: أنت حر بعد موت فلان، فهو مدبر مقيد، لكن في "المبسوط" وغيره: أنه ليس تدبيراً بل حتى لو مات فلان، والمولى حي عتق من كل المال، ولو مات المولى أولاً بطل التعليق. قال العيني ومن المقيد أن يقول: إذا مت وغسلت فأنت حر؛ لأنه علقه بالموت وشيء آخر بعده، فإن مات ففي القياس أن لا يعتق ما لم يغسل وإن غسل؛ لأنه لما لم يعتق بنفس الموت انتقل إلى الوارث، وفي الاستحسان يعتق؛ لأنه يغسل عقيب موته قبل أن يتقرر ملك الوارث فيه. ومنه أن يقول: أنت حر قبل موتي بشهر أو بيوم، ثم مات بعد شهر قال بعضهم: يعتق من ثلث المال، وقال بعضهم: يعتق من جميع المال وهو الصحيح؛ لأن العتق على قول أبي حنيفة يستند إلى أول شهر قبل الموت وهو كان صحيحاً في ذلك الوقت ولو مات قبل شهر لم يعتق؛ لأنه مدبر مقيد والقيد لم يوجد. ويعتق إن وجد الشرط: أي يعتق المدبر المطلق والمقيد والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى مثل: أنت حر بعد موت فلان من جميع المال إذا وجد الشرط، ويبطل التعليق بموت المولى قبل وجود الشرط كما لو قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت حر فمات المولى قبل الدخول. والحاصل أن المدبر المطلق والمقيد لابد أن يكون عتقه معلقاً بموت المولى، إما مطلقاً أو مقيداً بشيء آخر من وصف أو نحوه، أما المعلق عتقه على شرط فلا دخل لموت المولى في التعليق أصلاً، والمدبر بقسميه يعتق من الثلث، والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى يعتق من جميع المال، ونبه بقوله: "إن وجد الشرط" على أنه لابد أن يموت من مرضه هذا أو سفره أو في المدة المعينة، فلو أقام أو صح أو مضت المدة ثم مات لم يعتق؛ لبطلان اليمين قبل الموت.
He is sold if he says: This is a beginning of explaining the ruling of the restricted mudabbar, meaning if he says to his slave: If I die from this illness or in this journey, you are free; or if he says: If I die within ten years, you are free, then he is not an absolute mudabbar but a restricted mudabbar, and his sale is permitted by consensus because the cause is not concluded at present due to its being conditioned on that attribute, unlike the absolute mudabbar because his emancipation is attached to death. And it is restricted to ten years; because if he says: to one hundred years, and generally he does not live to that age, then it is an absolute mudabbar according to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Abu Yusuf said: It is not absolute because consideration is given to the timing, and the chosen view is the first because if he generally does not live to that age, it becomes as if it is inevitable, so his sale is not permitted. Or to ten years: meaning or if he says: If I die within ten years, you are free. Or you are free after the death of so-and-so: meaning if he says: You are free after the death of so-and-so, he is a restricted mudabbar, but in al-Mabsut and others: it is not tadbir; until if so-and-so dies and the master is alive, he is freed from all the wealth, and if the master dies first, the suspension is void. Al-Ayni said: And from the restricted is that he says: If I die and am washed, you are free; because he attached it to death and something after it. If he dies, analogically he is not freed until he is washed, even if washed, because having not been freed by death itself, he transfers to the heir; by istihsan he is freed because he is washed immediately after his death before the heir's ownership is established. And from it is that he says: You are free a month or a day before my death, then he dies after a month; some said: he is freed from one-third of the wealth, some said: from all the wealth, and this is correct because emancipation according to Abu Hanifa goes back to the beginning of the month before death, and he was healthy at that time, and if he dies before a month, he is not freed because he is a restricted mudabbar and the condition is not found. He is freed if the condition is found: meaning the absolute mudabbar, the restricted mudabbar, and him whose emancipation is suspended on a condition other than the master's death, such as you are free after the death of so-and-so, are freed from all the wealth if the condition is found, and the suspension becomes void upon the master's death before the condition is found, as if he said: If you enter the house, you are free, and the master dies before entrance. The summary is that the absolute and restricted mudabbar must have their emancipation attached to the master's death, either absolutely or restricted by another attribute; as for him whose emancipation is suspended on a condition, the master's death has no bearing on the suspension, and both types of mudabbar are freed from one-third, while the suspended one is freed from all the wealth. The statement 'if the condition is found' indicates that he must die from this illness or journey or within the specified period; if he travels on, recovers, or the period passes and then dies, he is not freed because the oath becomes invalid before death.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq dealing with restricted tadbir and suspended emancipation. It begins by explaining the matn's phrase 'and he is sold if he says...' — i.e., the slave can be sold if the master's declaration is restricted (muqayyad), such as 'if I die from this illness' or 'in this journey' or 'within ten years'. In these cases, the tadbir is restricted because the cause (death) is conditional on a specific attribute, so the slave is not yet fully mudabbar; hence sale is permitted by consensus. In contrast, absolute tadbir (e.g., 'you are free when I die') makes the slave a full mudabbar, not sellable. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the master says 'if I die within one hundred years' — which is unlikely — Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it absolute tadbir (so no sale), while Abu Yusuf considers it restricted (sale allowed). The preferred view is the first, because the condition is practically inevitable. The commentary then discusses other cases: saying 'you are free after the death of Zaid' — this is a restricted tadbir according to some, but in al-Mabsut it is not tadbir at all; rather it is a suspended emancipation (ta'liq) which frees from all wealth if the condition (Zaid's death) occurs before the master's death; if the master dies first, the suspension is void. Al-Ayni adds a case: 'if I die and am washed, you are free' — analogically (qiyas) the slave is not freed until washed, because after death without washing the slave goes to the heir; by istihsan he is freed immediately because washing happens right after death before ownership transfers. Another case: 'you are free a month before my death' — if the master dies a month later, some say freed from one-third; the correct view (endorsed by Abu Hanifa) is from all wealth because the freedom is retroactive to the beginning of the month when the master was alive. The commentary concludes that the matn's phrase 'if the condition is found' means that for a restricted mudabbar (e.g., 'if I die from this illness'), the slave's freedom depends on the master actually dying from that specific cause; if he recovers or the period passes, the slave is not freed.

Key Terms
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A slave whose tadbir is conditional on a specific attribute, e.g., death from a particular illness.
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar mutlaq): A slave declared free upon the master's death without any condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says, 'If I die from this illness, you are free,' the slave is:
A) An absolute mudabbar and cannot be sold.
B) A restricted mudabbar and can be sold.
C) Not a mudabbar.
D) Free immediately.

Key Takeaway
A restricted mudabbar can be sold, but if the condition is practically inevitable (e.g., 100 years), it becomes absolute and cannot be sold.

Distinguishing Tadbir from Suspended Emancipation (Ta'liq)
Expands on cases that distinguish tadbir from ta'liq, including istihsan applications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify cases of ta'liq (suspended emancipation) and distinguish them from tadbir, and apply the rules regarding source of wealth and condition fulfillment.

Core Idea
If freedom is conditioned on an event other than the master's death, it is ta'liq, not tadbir, and frees from all wealth.

This passage explores further formulations: 'You are free after Zaid's death', 'If I die and am washed', 'You are free a month before my death'. These reveal the boundary between tadbir and ta'liq, and the application of istihsan over qiyas. Let's examine each case and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the 'after Zaid dies' case
If the master says 'You are free after Zaid dies', this is not tadbir but suspended emancipation (ta'liq). The slave is freed from all wealth if the condition (Zaid's death) occurs before the master's death. If the master dies first, the suspension is void.
Text: 'في المبسوط وغيره: أنه ليس تدبيراً'.
2
Contrast with tadbir
Tadbir requires emancipation to be attached to the master's death, either absolutely or with a condition on death. Ta'liq has no connection to the master's death.
3
Analyze the washing case
If the master says 'If I die and am washed, you are free', analogically (qiyas) the slave is not freed until washed because after death without washing, ownership passes to heirs. By istihsan, he is freed immediately because washing happens right after death before ownership transfers.
Qiyas vs istihsan dispute.
4
Analyze the month-before case
If the master says 'You are free a month before my death' and dies a month later, some say freed from one-third; the correct view (Abu Hanifa) is from all wealth because freedom retroactively applies to the beginning of the month when master was alive.
Two opinions, preferred is from all wealth.
5
Summarize the distinction
Review the summary in the text: tadbir (absolute or restricted) attaches to master's death, frees from one-third. Ta'liq attaches to other conditions, frees from all wealth. The condition for tadbir freedom must be specifically fulfilled (e.g., dying from that illness).

ويباع لو قال: هذا شروع في بيان حكم المدبر المقيد يعني إذا قال لعبده إن مت من مرضي هذا أو في سفري هذا فأنت حر، أو قال: إن مت إلى عشر سنين فأنت حر فليس بمدبر مطلق بل هو مدبر مقيد يجوز بيعه بالإجماع؛ لأن السبب لم ينعقد في الحال؛ لتردده في تلك الصفة، بخلاف المدبر المطلق؛ لأن عتقه تعلق بالموت، وقيد بعشر سنين؛ لأنه لو قال: إلى مائة سنة، ومثله لا يعيش إليه غالباً فهو مدبر مطلق عند الحسن ابن زياد، وقال أبو يوسف: ليس بمطلق؛ لأن العبرة للتوقيت، والمختار هو الأول؛ لأنه إذا كان في الغالب لا يعيش إليه يصير كالكائن لا محالة، فلا يجوز بيعه. أو إلى عشر سنين: أي أو قال: إن مت إلى عشر سنين فأنت حر. أو أنت حر بعد موت فلان: أي لو قال: أنت حر بعد موت فلان، فهو مدبر مقيد، لكن في "المبسوط" وغيره: أنه ليس تدبيراً بل حتى لو مات فلان، والمولى حي عتق من كل المال، ولو مات المولى أولاً بطل التعليق. قال العيني ومن المقيد أن يقول: إذا مت وغسلت فأنت حر؛ لأنه علقه بالموت وشيء آخر بعده، فإن مات ففي القياس أن لا يعتق ما لم يغسل وإن غسل؛ لأنه لما لم يعتق بنفس الموت انتقل إلى الوارث، وفي الاستحسان يعتق؛ لأنه يغسل عقيب موته قبل أن يتقرر ملك الوارث فيه. ومنه أن يقول: أنت حر قبل موتي بشهر أو بيوم، ثم مات بعد شهر قال بعضهم: يعتق من ثلث المال، وقال بعضهم: يعتق من جميع المال وهو الصحيح؛ لأن العتق على قول أبي حنيفة يستند إلى أول شهر قبل الموت وهو كان صحيحاً في ذلك الوقت ولو مات قبل شهر لم يعتق؛ لأنه مدبر مقيد والقيد لم يوجد. ويعتق إن وجد الشرط: أي يعتق المدبر المطلق والمقيد والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى مثل: أنت حر بعد موت فلان من جميع المال إذا وجد الشرط، ويبطل التعليق بموت المولى قبل وجود الشرط كما لو قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت حر فمات المولى قبل الدخول. والحاصل أن المدبر المطلق والمقيد لابد أن يكون عتقه معلقاً بموت المولى، إما مطلقاً أو مقيداً بشيء آخر من وصف أو نحوه، أما المعلق عتقه على شرط فلا دخل لموت المولى في التعليق أصلاً، والمدبر بقسميه يعتق من الثلث، والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى يعتق من جميع المال، ونبه بقوله: "إن وجد الشرط" على أنه لابد أن يموت من مرضه هذا أو سفره أو في المدة المعينة، فلو أقام أو صح أو مضت المدة ثم مات لم يعتق؛ لبطلان اليمين قبل الموت.
He is sold if he says: This is a beginning of explaining the ruling of the restricted mudabbar, meaning if he says to his slave: If I die from this illness or in this journey, you are free; or if he says: If I die within ten years, you are free, then he is not an absolute mudabbar but a restricted mudabbar, and his sale is permitted by consensus because the cause is not concluded at present due to its being conditioned on that attribute, unlike the absolute mudabbar because his emancipation is attached to death. And it is restricted to ten years; because if he says: to one hundred years, and generally he does not live to that age, then it is an absolute mudabbar according to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Abu Yusuf said: It is not absolute because consideration is given to the timing, and the chosen view is the first because if he generally does not live to that age, it becomes as if it is inevitable, so his sale is not permitted. Or to ten years: meaning or if he says: If I die within ten years, you are free. Or you are free after the death of so-and-so: meaning if he says: You are free after the death of so-and-so, he is a restricted mudabbar, but in al-Mabsut and others: it is not tadbir; until if so-and-so dies and the master is alive, he is freed from all the wealth, and if the master dies first, the suspension is void. Al-Ayni said: And from the restricted is that he says: If I die and am washed, you are free; because he attached it to death and something after it. If he dies, analogically he is not freed until he is washed, even if washed, because having not been freed by death itself, he transfers to the heir; by istihsan he is freed because he is washed immediately after his death before the heir's ownership is established. And from it is that he says: You are free a month or a day before my death, then he dies after a month; some said: he is freed from one-third of the wealth, some said: from all the wealth, and this is correct because emancipation according to Abu Hanifa goes back to the beginning of the month before death, and he was healthy at that time, and if he dies before a month, he is not freed because he is a restricted mudabbar and the condition is not found. He is freed if the condition is found: meaning the absolute mudabbar, the restricted mudabbar, and him whose emancipation is suspended on a condition other than the master's death, such as you are free after the death of so-and-so, are freed from all the wealth if the condition is found, and the suspension becomes void upon the master's death before the condition is found, as if he said: If you enter the house, you are free, and the master dies before entrance. The summary is that the absolute and restricted mudabbar must have their emancipation attached to the master's death, either absolutely or restricted by another attribute; as for him whose emancipation is suspended on a condition, the master's death has no bearing on the suspension, and both types of mudabbar are freed from one-third, while the suspended one is freed from all the wealth. The statement 'if the condition is found' indicates that he must die from this illness or journey or within the specified period; if he travels on, recovers, or the period passes and then dies, he is not freed because the oath becomes invalid before death.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq dealing with restricted tadbir and suspended emancipation. It begins by explaining the matn's phrase 'and he is sold if he says...' — i.e., the slave can be sold if the master's declaration is restricted (muqayyad), such as 'if I die from this illness' or 'in this journey' or 'within ten years'. In these cases, the tadbir is restricted because the cause (death) is conditional on a specific attribute, so the slave is not yet fully mudabbar; hence sale is permitted by consensus. In contrast, absolute tadbir (e.g., 'you are free when I die') makes the slave a full mudabbar, not sellable. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the master says 'if I die within one hundred years' — which is unlikely — Hasan ibn Ziyad considers it absolute tadbir (so no sale), while Abu Yusuf considers it restricted (sale allowed). The preferred view is the first, because the condition is practically inevitable. The commentary then discusses other cases: saying 'you are free after the death of Zaid' — this is a restricted tadbir according to some, but in al-Mabsut it is not tadbir at all; rather it is a suspended emancipation (ta'liq) which frees from all wealth if the condition (Zaid's death) occurs before the master's death; if the master dies first, the suspension is void. Al-Ayni adds a case: 'if I die and am washed, you are free' — analogically (qiyas) the slave is not freed until washed, because after death without washing the slave goes to the heir; by istihsan he is freed immediately because washing happens right after death before ownership transfers. Another case: 'you are free a month before my death' — if the master dies a month later, some say freed from one-third; the correct view (endorsed by Abu Hanifa) is from all wealth because the freedom is retroactive to the beginning of the month when the master was alive. The commentary concludes that the matn's phrase 'if the condition is found' means that for a restricted mudabbar (e.g., 'if I die from this illness'), the slave's freedom depends on the master actually dying from that specific cause; if he recovers or the period passes, the slave is not freed.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending emancipation on a condition unrelated to the master's death, e.g., 'if Zaid dies'.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbar muqayyad): A slave whose tadbir is conditional on a specific attribute, e.g., death from a particular illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says, 'You are free after Zaid dies,' and Zaid dies while the master is alive, the slave is freed from:
A) One-third of the wealth (as a restricted mudabbar).
B) All the wealth (as suspended emancipation).
C) Nothing, because it is not a valid declaration.
D) Half the wealth.

Key Takeaway
Ta'liq (suspended emancipation) is not tadbir; it frees from all wealth and is void if the master dies before the condition.

Definition and Types of Tadbir: Mutlaq and Muqayyad
Definitions and examples of tadbir types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadbir, distinguish between absolute and restricted mudabbir, and state the ruling on selling a restricted mudabbir.

Core Idea
Tadbir ties freedom to the master's death; wording affects permissibility of sale and source of wealth.

Tadbir is a unique contract where the master declares his slave will be free upon his death. The exact wording—whether absolute or tied to an additional condition—determines the legal status of the slave (mudabbir). This lesson unpacks the key definitions and their immediate legal consequences, including the permissibility of sale and the share of wealth from which the slave is freed.

Guided Path
1
Define tadbir
Identify tadbir as a declaration linking freedom to the master's death. The slave becomes a mudabbir.
Tadbir is distinct from other ta'liq (suspension) where the condition is not the master's death.
2
Distinguish mutlaq and muqayyad
Use the examples: 'you are free after the death of so-and-so' is a restricted tadbir; 'you are free before my death by a month' is also restricted. The restriction is an additional condition beyond death.
Absolute tadbir is simply 'you are free when I die'.
3
Identify the ruling on sale
A restricted mudabbir may be sold, as stated in the commentary, because he is not an absolute mudabbir. An absolute mudabbir typically cannot be sold.
This difference is based on the degree of linkage to the master's death.
4
Note the wealth source
Both absolute and restricted mudabbir are freed from one-third of the master's wealth upon fulfillment of the condition, not from all wealth.
This distinguishes them from ta'liq on a non-death condition, which frees from all wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير
أو إلى عشر سنين، أو أنت حر بعد موت فلان، ويعتق إن وجد الشرط.

(ط، عيني)] أي لو قال: أنت حر بعد موت فلان، فهو مدير مقيد، لكن في "المبسوط" وغيره: أنه ليس تدبيراً بل حتى لو مات فلان، والمولى حي عتق من كل المال، ولو مات المولى أولاً بطل التعليق، وعبارة أصل الكنز أي "الوافي": "أنت حر إن مات فلان أو أنا" ، فالظاهر أن الأصل في عبارة المصنف هكذا: "أو أنت . موتي أو موت فلان"، فتحرفت.

(عيني، فتح) ويعتق إن وجد الشرط بأن مات من مرضه ذاك أو سفره ذاك (عيني)] أي يعتق المدبر المطلق والمقيد والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى مثل: أنت حر بعد موت فلان من جميع المال إذا وجد الشرط، ويبطل التعليق بموت المولى قبل وجود الشرط كما لو قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت حر فمات المولى قبل الدخول. والحاصل أن المدبر المطلق والمقيد لابد أن يكون عتقه معلقاً بموت المولى، إما مطلقاً أو مقيداً بشيء آخر من وصف أو نحوه، أما المعلق عتقه على شرط فلا دخل لموت المولى في التعليق أصلاً، والمدبر بقسميه يعتق من الثلث، والمعلق عتقه بشرط غير موت المولى يعتق من جميع المال، ونبه بقوله: "إن وجد الشرط" على أنه لابد أن يموت من مرضه هذا أو سفره أو في المدة المعينة، فلو أقام أو صح أو مضت المدة ثم مات لم يعتق؛ لبطلان اليمين قبل الموت. (فتح، عيني)
Chapter of Tadbir
Or to ten years, or you are free after the death of so-and-so, and he becomes free if the condition is found.
That is, or he said: you are etc.
Or to ten years: that is, or he said: if I die to etc. then you are free. (Ayni) After the death of so-and-so: if he said you are free if so-and-so dies or if I die and so-and-so dies; because he is not an absolute mudabbir, so his sale is permissible. (T, Ayni)] That is, if he said: you are free after the death of so-and-so, he is a restricted mudabbir, but in al-Mabsut and others: it is not tadbir; rather, even if so-and-so dies while the master is alive, he becomes free from all the wealth, and if the master dies first, the ta'liq becomes void. The expression of the original Kanz, i.e. al-Wafi: 'You are free if so-and-so dies or I', so apparently the original expression of the author was: 'or you: my death or the death of so-and-so', then it was corrupted.
Ta'liqan
Free after
al-Ayni said: Among the restricted is that he says: when I die and am washed, then you are free; because he suspended it on death and something else after it. If he dies, then by qiyas he does not become free unless he is freed and washed, because since he did not become free by death itself, he passes to the heir; but by istihsan he becomes free, because he is washed immediately after his death before the heir's ownership is established over him. Among this is that he says: you are free before my death by a month or a day, then he dies after a month. Some said: he becomes free from one third of the wealth, and some said: from all the wealth, and that is correct; because manumission according to Abu Hanifa is retroactive to the beginning of the month before death, and he was healthy at that time. If he died before the month, he does not become free, because he is a restricted mudabbir and the condition is not found, contrary to Zufar. (Ayni, Fath) He becomes free if the condition is found, by dying from that illness or that travel (Ayni)] That is, the absolute and restricted mudabbir, and the one whose manumission is suspended on a condition other than the master's death—such as 'you are free after the death of so-and-so'—become free from all the wealth if the condition is found, and the ta'liq becomes void by the master's death before the condition occurs, as if he said 'if you enter the house then you are free' and the master died before entry. The summary: the absolute and restricted mudabbir must have their manumission suspended on the master's death, either absolutely or restricted by another description or the like. As for the one whose manumission is suspended on a condition, the master's death has no role in the suspension at all. The mudabbir in both types becomes free from one third; the one whose manumission is suspended on a condition other than the master's death becomes free from all the wealth. He pointed out by his saying 'if the condition is found' that he must die from this illness or travel or within the specified period; if he recovers, becomes healthy, or the period passes and then he dies, he does not become free, because the oath becomes void before death. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the types and conditions of tadbir (manumission contingent on the master's death). The author first clarifies the different wordings that constitute tadbir: 'to ten years' or 'you are free after the death of so-and-so' are examples of restricted tadbir. The rule is that the slave becomes free only if the condition (the master's death from that illness or travel, etc.) is fulfilled. The commentary then details the difference between absolute and restricted tadbir, and how they differ from ta'liq (suspension) on a condition other than death. A key point is that the mudabbir (whether absolute or restricted) is freed from one-third of the master's wealth, whereas a slave whose manumission is suspended on a non-death condition is freed from all wealth. The passage also discusses istihsan in a case where the master says 'when I die and am washed'. By qiyas, the slave would not be freed because the washing occurs after death, but by istihsan, he is freed because washing follows immediately before the heir's ownership is established. Finally, the text mentions a disagreement with Zufar regarding a condition like 'you are free before my death by a month': Abu Hanifa holds that if the master dies after the month, the slave is freed from all wealth because the manumission is retroactive to the beginning of the month when the master was healthy; Zufar disagrees. The relied-upon position is the one stated in the text.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract where the master declares that the slave will be free upon the master's death.
مدبر مقيد (mudabbir muqayyad): A mudabbir whose manumission is tied to the master's death plus an additional condition (e.g., 'after the death of so-and-so').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on selling a restricted mudabbir?
A) It is permissible because he is not an absolute mudabbir.
B) It is not permissible because he is a mudabbir.
C) It depends on whether the restriction is a time limit.
D) It is always permissible for any mudabbir.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir requires the master's death as the condition; wording that only mentions another's death is not tadbir, and the rules differ.

Definition of Istilad and Basic Rulings on Umm Walad
Definition of istilad and initial rulings on umm walad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of istilad, identify the two ways it occurs, and apply the ruling that an umm walad cannot be sold.

Core Idea
An umm walad cannot be sold; her ownership is restricted until her master dies.

This lesson introduces the chapter on istilad (seeking a child from a slave concubine). You will learn the precise legal definition of istilad, the two circumstances that make a slave woman an umm walad, and the key ruling that an umm walad cannot be sold. Understanding this ruling is essential, as it distinguishes the umm walad from ordinary slaves and has practical implications for ownership and disposition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic and legal definition of istilad
Istilad literally means 'seeking a child'; legally, it is the master's act of seeking a child from his slave concubine, which gives her the status of umm walad.
The term combines the idea of procreation and legal status.
2
Identify the two ways istilad occurs
First, the master claims a child from his own slave concubine, whether she is a bondwoman (qinn) or a mudabbara. Second, a man marries a slave woman who has already borne his child; this corrupts the marriage and makes her umm walad without a separate claim.
In the second case, the marriage is automatically corrupted (fasad), not annulled, because the man now owns her as an umm walad.
3
Recognize the term 'umm walad' as a predominant name
The term is a 'ghalibah' (predominant) name, meaning it is a specific usage applied to a slave concubine who bears her master's child, similar to 'al-bayt' for the Kaaba or 'al-najm' for a specific star.
This linguistic point emphasizes that the term has a fixed legal meaning.
4
Apply the ruling 'lam tumlak' (she is not owned)
The text reads 'lam tumlak' with tashdid, meaning it is not permissible to transfer ownership of her. This prohibition covers sale, gift, and any other transfer of ownership. An exception is if she gives birth from someone else, then sale is permissible.
The exception confirms that her status is tied to bearing her master's child.
5
Note the permissibility of cohabitation and use
The master may cohabit with her, use her services, and benefit from her earnings (kasb), 'uqr (compensation for intercourse), and arsh (blood money for injury) because his ownership remains intact, similar to a mudabbara.
Marriage of the umm walad to another is allowed only after istibra' (waiting one menstrual period) and is recommended (nadb), not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستيلاد : [هو طلب الولد لغة وشرعا طلب الولد من الأمة. (عيني)) الاستيلاد يحصل بشيئين: أحدهما: أن ب يدعي السيد ولد أمته قنة كانت أو مدبرة والثاني: أن يملك الزوج زوجته الأمة التي ولدت منه، فإنه يفسد النكاح، وتصير أم ولده بلا دعوة، وأم الولد اسم للأمة المستولدة فهو من أسماء الغالبة، والغلبة عبارة عن قصر اللفظ العام على بعض أفراده في الاستعمال كالحج والتيمم ونظيره البيت والنجم. (عيني، فتح) لم تملك بالتشديد أي لا يجوز تمليكها ولو ولدت من غيره يجوز بيعها وتمليكها اتفاقاً. (ط، عيني) وتوطأ وتستخدم إلخ أي يجوز للمولى أن يتصرف في أم الولد هذه التصرفات؛ لأن الملك فيها قائم فأشبهت المدبر، وفيه إيماء إلى أن الكسب والعقر وأرش الجناية له. وتزوج بعد الاستبراء ندبا لبقاء ملكه. (عيني)
Chapter of Istilad: [Istilad is seeking a child linguistically and legally: seeking a child from a slave concubine. (Ayni) Istilad occurs by two things: one: the master claims a child of his slave concubine, whether she is a bondwoman or a mudabbara; the second: a man marries his wife who is a slave concubine who gave birth from him, then the marriage is corrupted, and she becomes umm walad without claim. Umm walad is a name for the slave concubine who has borne a child; it is a predominant name. Predominance means restricting a general word to some of its individuals in usage, like hajj, tayammum, and similarly al-bayt, al-najm. (Ayni, Fath) 'She is not owned' with emphasis i.e., it is not permissible to give her away; if she gave birth from someone else, selling her and giving her away is permissible by agreement. (T, Ayni) 'And she is cohabited, used, etc.' i.e., the master may perform these actions with the umm walad because his ownership remains in her, so she resembles the mudabbara. This implies that her earnings, blood money for injury, and compensation for loss are for him. 'And she is married after istibra' as a recommendation because his ownership remains. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage defines the chapter on istilad (seeking a child from a slave concubine). The author explains that istilad occurs in two ways: (1) the master claims a child from his own slave concubine, regardless of whether she is a simple bondwoman or a mudabbara (one whose freedom is promised upon the master's death), or (2) a man marries a slave woman who has already borne him a child, in which case the marriage becomes corrupted and she automatically becomes umm walad without needing a separate claim. The term 'umm walad' is a predominant name, meaning it is a common expression that refers specifically to a slave concubine who has borne her master's child, just as 'al-bayt' refers to the Kaaba and 'al-najm' to a specific star. The ruling 'lam tumlak' (she is not owned) is read with tashdid, indicating that it is not permissible to transfer ownership of her; however, if she gave birth from someone other than her master, she may be sold. The master retains the right to cohabit with her, use her services, and earn from her, as his ownership is intact, similar to a mudabbara. Marriage of the umm walad is permissible only after istibra' (waiting for one menstrual period) and is recommended, not required, because her master's ownership remains.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm walad): A slave concubine who bears her master's child and thereby acquires special status: she cannot be sold, becomes free on her master's death, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling an umm walad according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is permissible
B) It is not permissible
C) It is recommended
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
An umm walad cannot be sold because her ownership is restricted; she becomes free only upon her master's death.

Establishing Lineage of an Umm Walad's Child
Ruling with proof on lineage for umm walad's children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for lineage attribution of an umm walad's child and explain the proof from hadith and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
First child of umm walad needs master's acknowledgment; later children automatic due to firash.

The lineage of a child born to an umm walad (slave-concubine) is not automatically established. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the first child and subsequent children. This lesson examines the ruling, the prophetic proof, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for the first child
Identify the condition: the master must explicitly acknowledge the child for lineage to be established.
Without acknowledgment, the child is not attributed to him.
2
State the ruling for subsequent children
Once the first child is acknowledged, the umm walad becomes a legal bed (firash), so later children are automatically attributed without further acknowledgment.
This is based on the hadith 'al-walad li al-firash'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis argue that if intercourse alone made her a firash, she would need to observe 'idda upon separation, which is not the case. Hence, acknowledgment is necessary.
The proof relies on the absence of 'idda.
4
Understand the opposing school's view
Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that intercourse alone establishes lineage, arguing it is more productive than marriage.
They analogize to the wife, where marriage contract suffices.
5
Identify the practical difference
In the Hanafi school, the first child is only attributed if the master acknowledges. In the other schools, acknowledgment of intercourse is sufficient.
This affects inheritance and custody.

Source Text

(عيني) بعده: أي بعد الولد الأول الذي اعترف به (ط) عيني) ثبت نسبه لسيده إلخ أي فإن جاءت بولد بعد الولد الأول مع الاعتراف به ثبت نسبه منه، وإن لم يعترف من غير دعوة؛ لأنه لما ادعى الولد الأول تعين الولد مقصوداً منها، فصارت فراشاً، وقال علي: "الولد للفراش"، وصارت كالمنكوحة، وقال الشافعي: يثبت إذا اعترف بالوطء وإن عزل عنها إلا أن يدعي أنه استبرأها بعد وطئها بحيضة؛ لأن في المنكوحة يثبت بالعقد المفضي إلى الولد بواسطة الوطء، فلأن يكون الوطء نفسه مع كونه أكثر إفضاء مثبتا للنسب أولى، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: أنه لا فراش بها؛ لأنها لو صارت فراشاً بالوطء لوجب بزوال فراشها ما عدة. فإذا كان كذلك لا يثبت إلا باعترافه ولو اعترف بالحمل، فإذا جاءت به لستة أشهر ثبت نسبه المتيقن بوجوده وقت الإقرار، ولا فرق بين أن يكون حياً أو ميتاً بعد ما استبان خلقه، وإن جاءت به لأكثر لم يثبت، وبوطئه في دبرها يلزم الولد عند مالك وأحمد، وبوجه ضعيف عند الشافعي. Then know that the lineage of her first child is not established unless the master acknowledges it, and this will come later. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'After him' i.e., after the first child whom he acknowledged. (T, Ayni) 'Lineage is established to his master' etc. i.e., if she brings a child after the first child with acknowledgment, its lineage is established from him, even if he does not acknowledge it, without claim; because when he claimed the first child, the child became the intended purpose from her, so she becomes a bed (farash). And 'Ali said: 'The child belongs to the bed.' So she becomes like a married woman. Al-Shafi'i said: lineage is established if he acknowledges intercourse even if he withdrew, unless he claims that he performed istibra' after intercourse with one menstrual cycle; because in a married woman, lineage is established by the contract leading to the child via intercourse. So it is more appropriate that intercourse itself, being more productive, establishes lineage. Malik and Ahmad also said this. Our proof: there is no bed for her; if she became a bed by intercourse, then upon the removal of her bed, she would have to observe 'idda. Since that is not the case, lineage is not established except by his acknowledgment. If he acknowledges pregnancy and she gives birth within six months, the lineage is established with certainty of its existence at the time of acknowledgment, whether the child is born alive or dead after its features are apparent. If she gives birth after more than six months, lineage is not established. By intercourse in the anus, the child is attributed to him according to Malik and Ahmad, and in a weak opinion according to al-Shafi'i. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/339] It is called... and it is negated by his denial, unlike the first. And she becomes free upon his death from all his wealth, and she (umm walad) does not work off for his creditor. If the umm walad of a Christian converts to Islam, she works off her value.

Commentary
This passage addresses the establishment of lineage for children of an umm walad. The first child is only attributed to the master if he explicitly acknowledges it. Once he acknowledges the first child, the umm walad becomes a 'farash' (bed) similar to a married woman, and subsequent children are automatically attributed to him without further acknowledgment. This is based on the hadith 'The child belongs to the bed.' The author contrasts the Hanafi position with that of al-Shafi'i, who holds that lineage is established by the mere act of intercourse with the slave concubine, regardless of acknowledgment. The Hanafis argue that since she is not a permanent bed, she would require 'idda if she were, but since she does not, acknowledgment is necessary. The text also mentions that if the master acknowledges pregnancy and the child is born within six months, lineage is certain; if later, not. It also notes that the umm walad becomes free from the master's entire estate, not from one-third, and is not liable to work off her value for the master's debts. Finally, if the umm walad of a non-Muslim master converts to Islam, she must work off her value to gain freedom.

Key Terms
فراش (firash): The legal bed/marriage that establishes lineage; for umm walad, it is created by acknowledging the first child.

C) Only if the master acknowledges intercourse.
D) Never; every child requires acknowledgment.

Key Takeaway
The first child of an umm walad requires explicit acknowledgment for lineage; later children are automatically attributed due to the legal bed (firash).

Umm Walad Freed Upon Master's Death
Ruling on umm walad emancipation and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the umm walad is freed from the entire estate and distinguish the cases where she must work off her value.

Core Idea
Umm walad is freed from all wealth, not one-third, and owes no work for debts.

This passage affirms a special status: an umm walad (slave who bore her master's child) becomes free immediately upon her master's death, and her freedom is not limited to one-third of the estate. She is also not required to work off her value for the master's creditors. However, if she converts to Islam while owned by a non-Muslim, or if her status as umm walad was established under different conditions, she may need to work off her value. Let's unpack the precise rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The passage begins with 'وعتقت بموته من كل ماله' – she becomes free upon his death from all his wealth. This establishes the core: the umm walad's freedom is comprehensive, covering the entire estate.
This overrides the general rule that bequests are limited to one-third.
2
Note the exception for debts
The next phrase 'ولم تسع أي أم الولد لغريمه' clarifies that she does not have to work off (saa'yah) for the master's creditors. Her freedom is absolute, not conditional on debt payment.
This is based on the practice that the Prophet forbade selling an umm walad for debt.
3
Examine the first special case
If the umm walad of a Christian master converts to Islam, she must work off her value (سعت في قيمتها). Here, conversion triggers a need to compensate because the non-Muslim master cannot retain a Muslim slave.
This is a form of forced manumission with compensation.
4
Examine the second special case
If a free woman gave birth in a marriage and later became a slave of the same man, or if she was a mudabbara, she is evaluated and must work off. These are situations where the umm walad status is not automatically recognized from the beginning.
Evaluation ensures fair compensation for the master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعتقت بموته من كل ماله، ولم تسع أي أم الولد لغريمه، ولو أسلمت أم ولد النصراني سعت في قيمتها، وإن ولدت بنكاح فملكها أو مدبرته قومها تعدل وسعت
And she becomes free upon his death from all his wealth, and she (umm walad) does not work off for his creditor. And if the umm walad of a Christian converts to Islam, she works off her value. And if she gave birth in a marriage and then he owned her, or his mudabbara, she is evaluated, adjusted, and works off.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage states a key ruling: the umm walad is freed from the master's entire estate upon his death, meaning she is not restricted to one-third of the wealth like a bequest. This is based on the hadith commanding that umm walad be freed and not sold for debts. Therefore, she does not have to work off her value for the master's creditors. However, if the umm walad belongs to a non-Muslim master and she embraces Islam, she must work off her value (saa'yah) to gain freedom. Similarly, if a woman gives birth while married to someone else and then the master later owns her, or if she is a mudabbara, she is evaluated and must work off her value. This shows that the status of umm walad is recognized with immediate freedom from the entire estate, but in cases of conversion or change of ownership, compensation is required.

Key Terms
سعاية (saa'yah): A payment or work required from a slave to earn freedom; here, the umm walad of a non-Muslim master must work off her value if she converts.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to a child fathered by her master.
مدبرة (mudabbara): A slave promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the umm walad upon the death of her master?
A) She is freed from one-third of the estate.
B) She is freed from the entire estate but must work off for creditors.
C) She is freed from the entire estate and does not work off for creditors.
D) She remains a slave unless the debts are paid.

Key Takeaway
Upon a master's death, his umm walad is freed from the entirety of his estate, with no obligation to work off debts.
